# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
There were many coordinate systems we could choose, 
but for our convenience, we have chosen a cartesian system.
And smartly, we have picked the one aligning the motion of our object. ^SmYmHTHl

In general, the contact force on an object due to a surface 
can be in any direction. But for our convenience, we decompose 
the contact force as FRICTION (parallel to the surface) and
NORMAL CONTACT FORCE (perpendicular to the surface) ^AyW0LaKA

If we analyze this, actually, it acts funny for small angles. That is because our assumption about friciton
is wrong! f = mu * N only when the force acting on the block is sufficient. Otherwise, it is actually EQUAL to
the applied force (remember? Static friction is self adjusting)

Often, we need to handle different cases seperately with self adjusting forces (since they change their direction
and magnitude) ^MVEPTe4j
